Statement of Wang Keren, Supervisor of Students Studying in Japan 93

Regarding the Disputes Over Student Affairs in Japan

The disputes over student affairs in Japan have long been reported in various newspapers. It is now known that Wang Keren, the supervisor of students studying in Japan, arrived in Shanghai on the Nagasaki Maru the day before yesterday. A reporter from the New Sound Society immediately visited Mr. Wang at the Great China Hotel. According to Mr. Wang, student affairs in Japan are extremely difficult to handle. Whenever students from any province encounter financial difficulties, they go to the supervisor's office for loans, all assuming that the supervisor's office is a government agency. How could it be that they would turn a deaf ear to the difficulties of their own country's students in a foreign land without offering assistance? Even provincial managers, when their province's public funds fail to arrive on time, often come to the supervisor's office to find a solution, also believing that the supervisor's office is an agency that manages all students studying abroad. Now that students from a certain province are in difficulty, the supervisor's office cannot easily shirk responsibility and ignore them. Such situations are very difficult to deal with. The current dispute is based on this. Here, I will briefly address three issues:

First, the issue of loans from the Nichi-Ka Gakkai (Japan-China Society). The Nichi-Ka Gakkai is essentially a private organization specializing in Japan-China educational affairs. In June of this year, Hunan and Jiangxi's public funds failed to arrive on schedule. Therefore, Deng Tianmin, the manager of Jiangxi Province, negotiated with the Nichi-Ka Gakkai for a loan of 5,000 yuan. The Jiangxi manager borrowed 3,000 yuan, and the Hunan manager borrowed 1,200 yuan, each writing their own promissory notes to collect the money themselves. I only signed the promissory notes as a guarantor. In addition to these 4,200 yuan, the supervisor's office also borrowed 800 yuan, originally intended to meet the urgent needs of Guangxi and Hubei's government-funded students. Later, upon receiving a telegram from the Ministry of Education approving the allocation of funds for the return travel expenses of government-funded students from Hunan, Guangxi, and other provinces, it was decided that the funds could be used flexibly for Guangxi students. Hubei Province had already received its own provincial funds, so there was no need to borrow further. Unexpectedly, Luo Yiqun, the manager of Guangdong Province, also came to borrow money, so I had no choice but to borrow the funds from the Nichi-Ka Gakkai again to meet Mr. Luo's urgent needs. The process included handwritten letters from the Hunan and Jiangxi managers, which can be verified. Moreover, Deng Tianming reported the loan progress at the student affairs meeting, which can be verified in the meeting minutes. This was not a deceitful act. I believe that I have made no mistakes and that there are no irregularities. Those who are unaware of this process have assumed that the supervisor's office received subsidies from the Japanese Cultural Affairs Department and that the Cultural Affairs Department entrusted the Nichi-Ka Gakkai with 5,000 yuan to help students studying abroad. I formally wrote to the Cultural Affairs Department to inquire about this. Mr. Tsuboue Teiji, the director of the department, officially replied that there was no such thing. All documents can be provided as evidence. As for whether the funds lent by the Nichi-Ka Gakkai came secretly from the Cultural Affairs Department, or whether there was any relationship with the Cultural Affairs Department, the Hunan and Jiangxi provincial managers and the supervisor's office were completely unaware when they went to borrow the funds. It was not until the recent dispute that I inquired with the director of the Japanese Cultural Affairs Department and learned that the funds lent by the Nichi-Ka Gakkai were borrowed from local sources, fearing that they would not be repaid on time, causing the Nichi-Ka Gakkai to struggle to cope. Therefore, they designated 5,000 yuan as a guarantee for the Nichi-Ka Gakkai. However, neither the Cultural Affairs Department nor the Nichi-Ka Gakkai mentioned this situation to the Hunan and Jiangxi provincial managers or the supervisor's office at the time. After learning about this, I questioned Director Tsuboue why he did not say a word to the supervisor at the beginning. Mr. Tsuboue insisted that it was a matter between the Cultural Affairs Department and the Nichi-Ka Gakkai and that there was no need to inform the supervisor's office. I expressed my deep dissatisfaction with this. Fortunately, the 1,200 yuan borrowed by the Hunan manager from the society and the 800 yuan borrowed by the supervisor's office and then lent to the Guangdong manager have all been repaid. Only Deng Tianmin's case has not yet been repaid, but the manager should repay the full amount soon. This is a formal loan and cannot be considered as accepting Japanese subsidies.

Second, the issue of central government funding to assist students. In April and May of this year, gold prices soared, and the domestic political situation was unstable. Students from Hunan, Guangxi, and other provinces, whether government-funded or self-funded, felt financial hardship. I reported the situation to the minister, who forwarded it to the Executive Yuan, requesting the allocation of large sums of money to facilitate their return home. I also telegraphed the Ministry of Education directly with the same request. Later, according to the minister's reply from the Executive Yuan, it was decided to instruct the Ministry of Finance to allocate funds, but the Ministry of Finance never allocated a single penny. Even the decision to assist students returning home was not limited to government-funded or self-funded students. Only the Ministry of Education replied in a telegram, stating that it could allocate 10,000 yuan in national currency from the Chong fund as travel expenses for government-funded students from Hunan and Guangxi, which was slightly different from the original plan decided by the Executive Yuan. After receiving this telegram, the supervisor's office believed that unequal treatment of government-funded and self-funded students would easily cause disputes. Therefore, it presented the situation to the minister nearby for approval, temporarily not publishing the telegram, hoping to personally return to China to explain the difficulties to the Ministry of Education in detail. I received the telegram on June 28, and I returned to China on July 3. On July 10, I met Minister Jiang and explained in detail the reasons why both government-funded and self-funded students must receive the same assistance. Minister Jiang agreed in person. Later, I met Director Sun of the Higher Education Department. He initially believed that the Ministry's order was limited to government-funded students based on the telegram presented by the supervisor's office. After rereading the original telegram, he knew that the original telegram had mentioned both government-funded and self-funded students. Therefore, he had no objection to my personal presentation. I believed that both Minister Jiang and Director Sun were responsible personnel of the Ministry of Education. Since they had agreed in person, it should be implemented accordingly. After returning to Japan, I selectively lent funds to students in financial difficulty, whether government-funded or self-funded, returning home or not, from the funds approved by the Ministry of Education to provide assistance. This approach was partly my duty and I could not sit idly by, and partly because I had already obtained the personal approval of Minister Jiang and Director Sun. Unexpectedly, I recently received instructions from the Ministry of Education stating that some of the expenses borrowed by these students would not be approved, which was completely unexpected. If the expenses borrowed by the students are untrue, I will of course be severely punished. If they are true, then since they have been approved by the Minister and Director in person but are not approved, there seems to be a misunderstanding. I will submit another report.

Third, the issue of students receiving the Boxer Indemnity funds. Those who are unaware of the truth in the instructions from the Ministry of Education believe that there are more than ten people who are not eligible to receive the Boxer Indemnity funds. In fact, among the eighteen people deemed ineligible by the Ministry of Education, four are deemed by the Ministry of Education to be graduates of specialized schools who should not continue to receive the Boxer Indemnity funds after entering university. However, over the years, there have been many cases where graduates of specialized schools have continued to receive funding for university studies. One person was mistakenly reported by the previous supervisor, which I had already reported and corrected. The Ministry did not check the original case and mistakenly deemed it ineligible. It has now been verified and approved for funding. Another person was a student who had already received funding at the university last year. The Ministry of Education found that the original case approved that year was for research in a specialized subject, but they are still receiving funding at the university. This was also deemed to be my mistake. In fact, the supervisor's office did not expect there to be such a case in the old case from a year ago. In addition, there are twelve people who are continuing their studies or internships. At the end of June, I received an order from the Ministry to submit their grades for review. Although the Ministry of Education issued an order in mid-July to suspend the Boxer Indemnity funds, it was not appropriate to include those whose grades were still pending review under the previous order. As for the approval of the Boxer Indemnity funds for Han Jingyuan and Dai Liangmo, there were also some twists and turns. I admit that I have some shortcomings in the procedures, but in reality, there is no irregularity at all. I dare to say and believe that. After Mr. Wang finished speaking, he showed all the original letters sent to the Ministry of Education, the embassy, political party departments, and the Japanese Cultural Affairs Department, as well as letters from Director Tsuboue Teiji of the Japanese Cultural Affairs Department and the managers of Hunan and Jiangxi provinces. It can be seen that student affairs in Japan are difficult to handle and cannot be described in words. It will also be difficult for those who become supervisors in the future. (New Sound Society)

Annual Meeting of the Chinese Society for the Advancement of Science and Art (3) 94

The fourth annual meeting of the Chinese Society for the Advancement of Science and Art was held at 9:00 AM on the 5th in the Biology Building of National Central University. More than 130 people, including Zhou Changshou, attended the meeting. Thirty important cases were passed, some concerning the development of the society itself, some concerning the promotion of cultural undertakings, and some concerning the study of the Three Principles of the People. In summary, they all contain significant meaning and mission for the future national construction and cultural prosperity under party rule. The meeting adjourned at 12:00 PM. In the afternoon, the members visited the Central Party Headquarters of the Kuomintang, the Central Military Academy, and the Central Political School. At noon on the 4th, they were hosted by the China Book Company, which also presented each member with a beautiful desk calendar. On the evening of the 4th, they were hosted by Minister Wang Boqun of the Ministry of Transportation. At noon on the 5th, He Bingsong, the chief editor of the Commercial Press, personally came to Nanjing to host the members and presented each person with a pocket diary as a souvenir. On the evening of the 5th, they attended a reception at the Municipal Government. Mayor Wei Daoming personally delivered a speech, followed by speeches by Zhu Yincqing, Hu Shuhua, and others. The gathering ended happily at around 9:00 PM. The passed cases are recorded below:

(1) Fundraising for the society's foundation. (2) Revitalizing the society's affairs. (3) The society should expedite the establishment of a Natural Science Research Institute. (4) Organizing a Research Association for Construction Issues. (5) Studying the Three Principles of the People. (6) Establishing the society's library. (7) Establishing a printing house in the capital. (8) Requesting the society to initiate the printing of the Siku Quanshu (Complete Library in Four Sections) to promote our country's inherent culture. (9) The society should solicit systematic scientific works for printing and provide appropriate remuneration to promote academic development. (10) Publishing nautical charts. (11) Distinguishing between arts and sciences in the title of the "Science and Art Magazine". (12) Requesting the society to establish a preparatory school for advanced studies in Japan. (13) The society should establish a Public Science Popularization Committee. (14) Establishing a "Career Introduction Department". (15) The standard for soliciting society fees should be the national currency commonly used in Shanghai, where the general headquarters is located. (16) Soliciting supporting members. (17) Regulations for academic inspection tours should be stipulated. (18) Purchasing houses in Beiping to build the Beiping branch office. (19) Revising the society's constitution. (20) Requesting the National Government to negotiate with the Japanese government as soon as possible to resolve the return of the Boxer Indemnity funds. (21) Requesting the National Government to allocate a large sum of money from the Boxer Indemnity funds returned by various countries to subsidize excellent private universities nationwide to enrich natural science equipment and library content, and to supplement academic groups' actual research in specialized academic fields. (22) Requesting the National Government to subsidize academic groups to establish natural science research institutes. (23) Requesting the National Government to instruct the competent authorities to hold entrance examination and testing to promote equal educational opportunities. (24) Requesting the National Government to order schools nationwide to emphasize natural sciences. (25) Uniting academic groups and cultural institutions in various countries to promote progress. (26) The society's future work should focus on the Three Principles of the People to promote science and art. (27) Suggesting the central government establish a central library. (28) Establishing a science and art middle school in the capital. (29) Requesting the National Government to instruct the Legislative Yuan to stipulate measures for using temple property to fund education and issue a notice to the whole country to proceed in a unified manner. (30) Raising funeral expenses for deceased members.

In addition, Hu Shuhua of the Engineering College of National Central University spoke on the spirit of creation, Xu Shimin spoke on the general situation of civil engineering in China in 1926, Li Daichen spoke on the properties of steel at high temperatures, and Nie Tanggu spoke on the preparatory work in China's construction process. Lu Guixiang of the College of Science spoke on aspects of radio waves, Chen Zhilin spoke on the study of West Lake sludge, Zheng Zhenwen spoke on the history of Chinese alchemy, Ma Zongrong of the College of Education spoke on library education, Shu Xincheng spoke on my views on education, He Bingsong spoke on my views on sorting out Chinese history, Liu Yunchou of the College of Agriculture spoke on the food problem and the burial system, and Yang Donglin of the Central Political School spoke on the issue of reducing provincial areas, etc.

First Meeting of Scout Leaders in the City 95

Twelve-hour hike to be held on the 14th

The Shanghai Boy Scout Council, in order to promote the Boy Scout cause in the city, convened its first meeting of scout leaders at the council at 2:30 PM yesterday. More than a dozen troop leaders and assistant troop leaders attended. Chairman Shen Yu, recorder Luo Lie. The meeting proceeded according to protocol: (1) The chairman reported on the significance of convening this meeting of troop leaders. (2) The troop leaders reported on the current work of their respective troops. (3) Discussion: (1) Determining the date for the 24-hour implementation case. (Resolved) Changed to 12 hours, scheduled for December 12-14. (2) Scheduling a citywide Boy Scout Party Righteousness Speech Conference. (Resolved) Scheduled for the anniversary of the death of the Premier next year. (3) How should the Boy Scouts of this city celebrate the 20th New Year's Day? (Resolved) A commemorative meeting will be held on the morning of New Year's Day, a film will be screened, and a Boy Scout dinner will be held in the evening. (4) How should the Boy Scouts be made to earnestly implement the maxim of "Doing a Good Deed Every Day"? (Resolved) Please ask the council to review the handling. (5) How should the families of Boy Scouts be made to have faith in Boy Scout training? (Resolved) Please ask the council to review the handling. (6) Future training of Boy Scouts should pay special attention to the implementation of the oath of allegiance. (Resolved) Please ask the council to review the handling. (5) Temporary motions. The 10th troop requested that the headquarters determine the date of the Chinese Boy Scout Memorial Day. (Resolved) Please ask the council to handle it. (6) Please ask the headquarters to consult with the railway and transportation departments to stipulate that Boy Scouts can purchase half-price boat and bus tickets when traveling. (Resolved) Please ask the council to handle it. (6) Adjournment.

Dispute Over the Ping Pong Champagne Cup Tournament 108

Jian De Refuses the Second Place Prize

To the Esteemed Editor,

We, the staff of the Champagne Cup Ping Pong Tournament of the Shanghai Race Club, humbly submit this letter. The primary aim of our organization in initiating the Champagne Cup tournament is to promote the sport of ping pong. Therefore, we have striven for perfection in all our measures. This year, we were honored by the enthusiastic participation of various teams, reaching a total of twenty-four. While some may attribute this to our organization's promotional efforts, we dare not take undue credit. The members of our organization have been diligently working to ensure the success of the event, especially given the increased number of participating teams. Fortunately, thanks to the understanding of the various teams, we were able to complete the event smoothly. We were greatly surprised by the sudden withdrawal of the Jian De team before the finals.

We have treated all teams equally, without any intention of discrimination. Therefore, we regret Jian De's unexpected action, both for the sake of their reputation and for the sake of the spirit of sportsmanship. We are compelled to record the details of the situation and submit them to your esteemed newspaper for publication, so that the public can understand the truth.

The number of seats for this final match was limited. To maintain order, all admission tickets were regulated. In addition to the ten complimentary tickets given to each team participating in the tournament, a certain number of tickets were also distributed to staff, referees, recorders, reporters, and so on. Therefore, the four hundred complimentary tickets prepared were quickly exhausted. The number of tickets for sale was also limited and equal to the number of complimentary tickets. Unexpectedly, the Jian De team requested as many as one hundred tickets. We immediately explained our predicament and were unable to grant them more than the ten tickets stipulated in the regulations. To our surprise, Lu Zhongqiu, a member of the Jian De team, tore up all the complimentary tickets, and the team captain, Lu Xiulu, did not prevent him. Such contempt for our organization and such a loss of personal integrity were rarely seen. However, we tried to handle it leniently, hoping that they would reflect on their actions. However, even after questioning, they did not realize their mistake and insisted that their team had cheerleaders, staff, advisors, etc. who required one hundred tickets. Such an unreasonable request is truly laughable, as we have never heard of cheerleaders, etc. needing to be given tickets.

In the interest of resolving the matter, our organization sent a letter to the team stating that during the competition, the players would be received on the field by our staff, and the torn tickets would not be investigated. However, the team did not understand and forgot their own actions. Until the day before the final (the 6th), they suddenly sent a letter requesting a postponement. As everything was already in place and the time was short, it was difficult to accommodate their request. Therefore, we immediately sent a reply and published a statement in the newspaper. As a result, the Jian De team was absent from the final match, and our organization's enthusiasm for promoting the sport was somewhat diminished, which is regrettable.

Now that the past is over, let us speak for Jian De. Is it worth it to withdraw because the request for tickets was not granted and the request for a postponement was denied? Alas, although ping pong is a minor sport, it has its own inherent value that cannot be taken lightly. We cannot help but lament this setback.

Respectfully submitted,

The Staff of the Champagne Cup Ping Pong Tournament of the Shanghai Race Club

The Shanghai Ping Pong Association Expresses Its Opinion

The Secretariat of the Shanghai Ping Pong Association issued an opinion regarding the Jian De team being ruled as having forfeited the match, stating that in yesterday's Champagne Cup final, Jian De and Tianma were evenly matched, and the outcome was difficult to predict. However, considering past performance and the talents of both sides, Jian De was actually superior to Tianma. Players of Jian De team such as Lu Xiulu, Lu Zhongqiu, Zhou Jianwen, Wang Bohong, Li Chuanshu, Guo Hai, etc. are all renowned Far Eastern players and rare talents in the ping pong world. Unexpectedly, news came that, due to a ticket dispute and correspondence with the Race Club, four days were spent without a resolution. It is said that when the Jian De team requested tickets from the association on Tuesday of last week, they had already stated that if the ticket issue was not resolved, the final on the 7th could not be held, and a postponement was requested. Unexpectedly, the association took a tough stance and used the championship as a constraint against the Jian De team. Because Jian De had won the championship in the previous competition by defeating Tianma six matches to one, Jian De believed that the club had lost the true spirit of promoting sports and wished to uphold the principle that athletes should not be driven by the concept of championships. Therefore, they decided to propose a postponement to the club so that the public could judge the matter. It is now reported that Jian De has been judged to have forfeited. The Tianma team has gained the championship without any effort, which is gratifying for Tianma, but also unfair to Jian De. Moreover, according to the competition rules, postponement of matches one day in advance was permitted by the club, as evidenced by the matches between Guangdong and Post A, and Japan and Jian De. Furthermore, the Jian De team had already informed the association on Tuesday that they would not compete if the issue was not resolved, and in their letter on Saturday, they informed the newspaper and the association of the reasons for requesting a postponement. Now, such an absurd and irrational judgment has been made. Is this not acting on impulse? Or is it favoring Guangdong and Japan while being unfair to Jian De? Or is there some other motive? It is regrettable that the public will not be able to see the skills of the Jian De team, and Tianma will not be able to display its power to avenge the defeat of six matches to one in the past. This championship seems to have been won in a shameful manner. If Tianma wishes to maintain its past glory, it should rise up and reject this type of appointed championship. If it does so, the reputation of the ping pong world will be greatly enhanced, adding luster to the sports world. It is heard that the Jian De team has decided to reject the second place prize offered by the club and is seeking public opinion.

Recent News on Sino-Russian Negotiations

To Meet with National Government Officials and Seek Instructions

The Sino-Russian negotiations resumed in Moscow on the 4th of this month. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has not yet received a report from Representative Mo Dehui. Recovering the Japanese Concession 112

Hankou...The Ministry of Foreign Affairs Has Not Yet Received a Reply from Japan

Wang Jiazhen's Remarks to Reporters Yesterday

Regarding the issue of recovering the Japanese concession in Hankou, the Japanese side has not yet made a formal statement after the Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued a note. Yesterday, a reporter from this newspaper interviewed Wang Jiazhen, Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs in Shanghai, for details. According to Wang, he had not yet discussed the recovery of the Japanese concession in Hankou with Japanese Ambassador Shigemitsu. Chen Shaokuan 114

Assumed Concurrent Post at the Shipyard Yesterday

Summoned Officials in the Morning for Instructions

Vice Director Chen Is Still Being Retained

Ma Deji, Director of the Jiangnan Shipyard, and Chen Zaofan, Vice Director, submitted requests to the Ministry of the Navy last month, asking for approval to resign due to the heavy losses incurred by the sharp rise in gold prices in recent years, which hindered operations. The vacant position was temporarily filled by Chen Shaokuan, Vice Minister of Naval Affairs. After arriving in Shanghai the day before yesterday, Chen received the shipyard's documents and assumed his duties at the shipyard at 8:00 AM yesterday (the 8th). At 9:00 AM, he summoned all officials for instructions, stating that he did not bring anyone or any money with him, and that although the economic situation of the Jiangnan Shipyard was extremely difficult, the shipyard was closely related to the navy and indirectly related to the country. When the Premier was in Japan, he had a grand plan for the construction of the navy in his Outline of National Reconstruction. The original intention of the state to have the Jiangnan Shipyard was to make money and expand the economy. Unfortunately, in recent years, it has suffered heavy losses due to various reasons. He was very pleased to be able to meet with everyone at this difficult time, when foreign shipyards in Shanghai are competing fiercely. He hoped that everyone would continue to work diligently and carefully, and that any ideas for reform could be communicated to him in person or in writing, and he would adopt them as much as possible. He would not cause panic due to the change of leadership. In the future, if the shipbuilding industry gradually prospers and develops, and the Premier's construction plan is realized, it would be beneficial not only to the country but also to everyone. At 9:30 AM, Chen was greeted by the former Vice Director Chen Zaofan and the foreign staff of the shipyard. In the afternoon, he began work without any ceremony. Chen is scheduled to return to Beijing tonight (the 9th). It is heard that Vice Director Chen Zaofan is still being retained.

The Taxpayers' Association Denies the Water Price Increase 115

Meeting Today to Discuss Draft Letter

The Shanghai Chinese Taxpayers' Association issued a notice yesterday, stating "Notice to all users of the Public Concession's tap water": Regarding the British Shanghai Waterworks Company's imposition of a 25% surcharge beginning September 1 of this year, the Association's representative meeting has resolved, based on the review of the company's account report, not to recognize the surcharge and has seriously negotiated with the Public Works Department. The Executive Committee has resolved to publish a notice to all users that all water prices should be paid at the old price (i.e., the price before August) before the negotiations are resolved. If water is cut off due to non-payment of the surcharge, please report it to the Association immediately. This notice is hereby issued on December 8, the 19th year of the Republic of China.

Another notice was sent to all executive committee members yesterday, stating: "We are scheduled to hold the seventh meeting of the Executive Committee at 2:30 PM on December 9 (Tuesday) at the Association's building to discuss the draft letter to the Public Works Department regarding the non-recognition of the water company's surcharge, etc. Please attend the meeting at that time."

China Merchants Bureau Suggests Transferring Previous Equity 116

Total Share Capital of 12.8 Million Taels

Takeover by the National Government with Funds Based on a Compromise

The Nichinichi Shimbun states that after the China Merchants Bureau was taken over and nationalized, special administrator Li Zhonggong was appointed to actively reorganize the bureau's internal and external affairs. However, the primary issue is how to transfer the equity of previous merchants to government control. Only after this issue is resolved can the remaining reorganization be carried out smoothly. The Design Committee of the China Merchants Bureau discussed this issue, stating that the China Merchants Bureau has a total share capital of 8.4 million taels, and the Jiyu Company has a total share capital of 4.4 million taels. The combined share capital of the two companies is 12.8 million taels. Each share originally cost 3 sets of silver, or 270 taels of silver. The current market value of each share is approximately 50 taels. If the government uses a compromise method of funding the takeover based on the original share value and the current market value, then a thorough reorganization after nationalization can be achieved in the near future, and expansion and construction can be carried out step by step. It is also speculated that most shareholders would be willing to have the National Government take over the equity using a compromise method, as the current market price of each share is only about 50 taels. It is difficult to determine whether the price can rise to 130 or 140 taels in a short period of time. The Design Committee has discussed this issue and made a sincere suggestion to the National Government, but it is not yet known whether the National Government will adopt it.

The Diplomatic Support Association for Chinese Citizens in the Netherlands Telegraphs the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to Negotiate the Xiao Case 117

The Diplomatic Support Association for Chinese Citizens in the Netherlands held its first general meeting at the Chinese Overseas Association yesterday, electing the Chinese Overseas Association and 50 other groups as executive committee members, and the Shanghai Municipal Party Committee and 20 other groups as supervisory committee members. After the election, the association sent a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in the name of the general meeting, requesting serious negotiations on the Xiao case. The text of the telegram is recorded below:

"To the esteemed Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing: According to reports, the Dutch ambassador stated in his conversation that the Dutch embassy has received letters from various parties regarding the Xiao Xin'an defamation case, but has not received a protest from your ministry. The Dutch ambassador witnessed your ministry's submission and therefore concluded that 'the matter will be resolved by the parties involved and will not become an international issue.' These few words, contrasting the heat of 'various parties' with the coldness of 'your ministry,' are enough to describe the shortcomings of your ministry. Because it is said that 'various parties' indicate that it is public outrage. If it is 'public outrage,' then your ministry should protest. However, your ministry likes what the people hate and hates what the people like, not only violating the nature of the people but also making the world laugh. Does your ministry, which is far removed from the people, know the enthusiasm of the whole country against the Netherlands? Last month, the Shanghai Anti-Dutch Assembly was attended by more than 100 groups and thousands of representatives. The highest academic institution was the Academia Sinica. The leaders of the mass movement were the Shanghai Municipal Party Committee. The national public opinion center was the Shanghai press. The famous mass organization was the Ningbo Native Place Association. The venue was the 'stable' Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce. The crowd had no 'irregularity.' Looking around, party and legal groups condemned the crime, not neglecting the distant. Magazines and newspapers attacked and satirized, not differing by factions. Literary scholars either cried in long songs or wrote tragedies. Workers and merchants either patrolled and boycotted or stopped work with generosity. Only your ministry was deaf and blind, indifferent and unconcerned. Are people all fools and your ministry alone wise? Are people all stupid and your ministry alone intelligent? If your ministry has no intention of flattering foreigners, the association deeply hopes that it will not be far before it restores its honor. Based on the resolutions of the Shanghai Anti-Dutch Assembly, the minimum requirements for the Xiao case are five: (1) The Dutch government must formally apologize to our government and guarantee that similar incidents will never happen again. (2) The Java Company must publish in Chinese and Western newspapers throughout China and all places where overseas Chinese reside, apologizing to our nation and Ms. Xiao, and guaranteeing that similar incidents will never happen again. (3) The first mate of the Chibad ship, Lan Anqi (H.W.L.vang), and the second mate, Lei Dima Kai (T.C. Rademakue), must be severely punished and not merely dismissed or demoted. (4) The shipowner, Yales (D.P. Als), and the ship's doctor, Bailing Gu (G.H. Bringow), must be permanently dismissed and not merely demoted or transferred. (5) Compensate Ms. Xiao for the loss of 100,000 taels. The Dutch side should be formally negotiated to relieve the doubts of all parties and clear the national shame. If they are attached to the Dutch court, despise public opinion, and sit on the opportunity to negotiate, further increasing the history of failure, our people, though weak, cannot forgive your ministry. Respectfully, the Diplomatic Support Association for Chinese Citizens in the Netherlands."

Supplementary Record of Mayor Zhang's Speech at the International Radio Station 118

The International Wireless Radio Station in Zhenru held an opening ceremony on the 6th. Mayor Zhang was ordered by the National Government and the Executive Yuan to attend as a representative. His speech was recorded in the previous newspaper. Now we have found the original manuscript and are re-publishing it below:

"Today, the International Wireless Radio Station is holding its opening ceremony. Yesterday, I received a telegram from the Civilian Affairs Office of the National Government, stating that Minister Wang requested that a representative be sent to guide the ceremony, and the Chairman instructed to send Mayor Zhang. I also received a telegram from the Executive Yuan, instructing me to attend as a representative. I am honored to attend this grand ceremony. Our country's telegraph began in the eighth year of Guangxu of the Qing Dynasty, and has a history of more than 50 years. However, in the Qing Dynasty, we focused on wired telegraph and did not pay attention to wireless telegraph. Although in the early years of the Republic of China, wireless stations were established in Shanghai, Wusong, Chongming, Wuchang, Guangzhou, Fuzhou, Beiping, and Zhangjiakou, domestic communication was still not smooth, let alone international communication. Therefore, our country relied on land lines and submarine cables for international telegrams. Land lines include the Sino-Russian line, such as from Hailanpao through Siberia to Moscow, or from Qiaaktu through Siberia to Moscow and then to various European countries. There is also the Sino-French line, such as from Yunnan through French Vietnam to various European countries, etc. All of these have lost their rights due to the impact of unequal treaties. Submarine cables include the Great Eastern, Great Northern, and Pacific companies, and Japan's Qingzu Yan, Da Hu Qi, and Kawashi Yamu to Tamsui four lines. The unequal treaties signed with our country, such as those concerning landing rights, transmission and reception rights, and apportionment fees, have severely infringed upon our country's telecommunications rights, which is well known to the people. The state's telecommunications are like the blood vessels of the human body. If it is held upside down and controlled by others, not only will rights flow out, but it will also be a hub for international political and economic aggression, which is extremely dangerous. In recent years, the people have paid attention to this. Therefore, the three northeastern provinces already have a large-scale international wireless telegraph station. Since the success of the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army and the establishment of the capital in Nanjing, it has been our responsibility to abolish unequal treaties. The contracts signed between telecommunications and international affairs are all naturally in the list of negotiating to abolish unequal treaties and revising equal treaties. On the one hand, we pay attention to establishing our own large-scale wireless station for international communication to maintain the independence of telecommunications and facilitate the transportation of telecommunications, so as not to be manipulated by foreigners. The Construction Committee established a large-scale wireless station in Shanghai the year before last, communicating with the United States via Little Luzon. Later, it was transferred to the Ministry of Communications. The Ministry of Communications also planned to establish a large wireless station in Shanghai to directly communicate with the United States, and after taking over, it immediately merged the plan, making the scale larger and the transmission faster. This is the current Zhenru International Wireless Radio Station. Since its preparation, it has been carefully managed, and all construction and layout are very complete. The excellent results of future international communication can be predicted. Today's opening ceremony is a celebration for the future of telecommunications. The efforts of Minister Wang and all those involved are evident. However, I also have something to add. Our country's telecommunications have been bound by unequal treaties for decades. After the pain, we have established this large-scale international wireless station. Not only will international communication be convenient from now on, but it will also promote the negotiation of abolishing unequal treaties, revising equal treaties, and recovering lost rights. I deeply hope that everyone will work hard, strive for perfection, and add a bright color to telecommunications and transportation. This is the long-term expectation that I, representing the National Government, representing Chairman Jiang, and representing the Executive Yuan, extend to you."

International Telecommunications Negotiations 119

Director Zhuang's Speech at the Telecommunications School

Zhuang Zhihuan, Director of the Telecommunications Department of the Ministry of Communications, inspected the Telecommunications School at 3:00 PM yesterday. He was guided to various places by Principal Wang Yuxiang and Dean Yu Bingjian. Wang and Yu requested that he give a speech on the progress of international telecommunications negotiations so that his colleagues could understand the truth. He immediately agreed, and all teachers and students attended the speech. Director Zhuang briefly stated that there have been many misunderstandings among colleagues regarding the recent international telecommunications negotiations, and even blame has been placed on individuals, which is deeply regrettable. The construction of submarine cables was agreed to by our former Qing government. On the one hand, there are legal restrictions, and on the other hand, there are economic benefits. In the past, Qing diplomacy was handled by the Prime Minister's Office for Foreign Affairs, and the contracts signed were full of jokes and many shortcomings. Legally, national rights were damaged, and the so-called economic benefits were only a kind of sovereignty tax. It is painful to say this. The old contract will expire at the end of this year. The content focuses on debt relations, such as the Shanghai-Yantai-Fuzhou submarine cable loan and the prepaid overseas reporting fees, totaling 4.4 million yuan in Chinese silver. Initially, the other party believed that our country's domestic political situation was unstable and there was no sincerity in the negotiations. Then, they used our economic constraints as a means of coercion. Moreover, the contracts of the Great Eastern, Great Northern, Pacific, and Japan's four companies will all expire at the end of this year. These companies are using international encirclement as a means, and their interests are all aimed at mutual observation, containment, and hindrance to the progress of negotiations. The issue of the loan has now been resolved by Minister Wang in consultation with the Shanghai banking community, who have temporarily advanced 5 million yuan. As for the issue of international communication, the international wireless station, which has been prepared for a long time, was officially opened on the 6th, and the results were extremely satisfactory. In the future, the signing of new contracts, such as patent rights, landing rights, transmission and reception rights, and reporting fees, will be within the scope of not hindering our national sovereignty, in order to seek the most favorable path. Progress is being made actively. The outcome is unknown, and it is impossible to guarantee satisfaction, but the abolition of the old contract should not be a problem. I deeply hope that my colleagues will work hard in their studies and do their best to improve telecommunications. Once the negotiations are over, the details will be announced.

An Overview of Internal and External Debt 121

Internal Debt Group Has Not Yet Held a Meeting

The Hua Dong News Agency states that the Ministry of Finance of the National Government has preparations for reorganizing internal and external debt, and the domestic banking community is organizing a creditor group and has appointed Zhang Gongquan of the Bank of China and four others as representatives of the creditor group. However, although these representatives have been appointed, they have not yet begun to carry out their work. Tan Danya of the Continental Bank and Zhou Zuomin of the Jin City Bank are currently going to Wuhan and returning to Beijing, respectively. Therefore, a formal meeting of the representatives is difficult to decide at this moment. However, according to Lin Kanghou, Standing Committee Member of the Banking Association, the two representatives' trip to the north is to attend to personal matters and they will come to Shanghai soon. All preparations for the creditor group are currently underway. According to a gentleman from the banking community speaking to a reporter from the Hua Dong News Agency, it is difficult to calculate the exact amount of internal and external debt. However, the only reliable source is the report of the Beijing government's financial reorganization meeting before the 16th year of the Republic of China. As of the end of the 14th year, the debt under the Ministry of Finance was 486,646,630.38 yuan for external debt and 266,150,800.38 yuan for internal debt, totaling 752,796,800.76 yuan. The debt under the Ministry of Communications was 561,967,765.37 yuan for external debt and 87,358,621.93 yuan for internal debt, totaling 649,326,387.30 yuan. The above calculation of external debt was based on the standard of 1 pound of British gold equaling 12 yuan of national currency and 1 US dollar equaling 2.4 yuan of national currency at that time. The total amount above is more than 140,000 yuan, and with the addition of interest from the 15th to 19th years and the current exchange rate of gold, it is feared that it is more than 200,000 yuan.

More Chinese Expelled from Japan 123

The crafting of mahjong tiles and the gambling associated with them are prevalent in the islands [of Japan]. Most of the tiles used are produced in Shanghai, then shipped for export. Recently, several Chinese workers involved in mahjong tile manufacturing, including Shi Huacui, Ju Jinbo, and Wang Xingchang, traveled from Shanghai to Japan with the intention of establishing mahjong tile shops and manufacturing tiles for sale. When Shi and the others arrived in Kobe by ship, they were detained by the Japanese Water Police, who feared they would encroach upon Japanese industry and livelihoods. They were not allowed to land and were deported back to Shanghai on the same ship. They returned to Shanghai yesterday in a very distressed state.

Among the Chinese from various trades who went to Kobe were Lin Shengji and Lin Yao, who were engaged in the kimono business. Upon arrival, they were immediately denied landing and were forced to return to Shanghai on the same ship. Also, Yang Rongqing and Lin Qingyu, who were from Fujian and were traveling to Tokyo, were also prevented from landing. Furthermore, Wei Jintao, Pan Yingen, Zhou Rengen, Lin Qihao, and six other workers in the catering and labor industries, who were traveling to the Shitaya district, Asakusa, and Fukushima Prefecture in Japan, were also deported back to Shanghai yesterday on the Tsukuba Maru. These Chinese, after arriving in Shanghai, are now reportedly residing in the Hongkou and Nanshi districts.

Record of the Second Children's Health Competition at the County People's Education Center 124

A total of sixty-three children participated in the competition.

The first prize overall went to Sun Heming, and the second prize went to Zhu Tiexi. The Shanghai County People’s Education Center held its second children's health competition for seven days, starting on the first of the month. The various details are recorded below. The final competition concluded at the center yesterday, and the details of the various events are recorded as follows.

Preliminary Results: The preliminary rounds were held from the first to the fifth of the month. The children were divided into groups in advance, and their health was examined on specific days. All the children reported on time. Local doctors Zhuang Weizhong and Huang Heng served as medical judges, while Wu Jingqing, Zhu Jiasheng, Liu Yunshu, and others served as judges for weight, height, and other health measurements. A total of sixty-three children qualified for the final competition. According to Zhuang Weizhong, the center’s health instructor, the children’s health levels were more uniform than in the previous competition, making it extremely difficult to judge their merits. Therefore, the judging panel decided to relax the quota and determine the final results during the final competition.

Final Competition: The final competition was held on the morning of the seventh. The families led their children to the venue. Starting at 9 a.m., the judges evaluated the children one by one in numerical order. On that day, renowned doctors from Shanghai, including Cai Yumen, Cheng Hanzhang, Jiang Zhenxun, and Cai Shicun, jointly attended the event to serve as judges for the final competition. The county normal school's Boy Scouts maintained order. More than a thousand guests attended. At the same time, a children’s health talk was held. The speakers included renowned doctors Cai Yumen, Cheng Hanzhang, Jiang Zhenxun, and Zhuang Changzhong. The audience was able to understand the content. After the talk, the final competition results were available. The total first prize went to Sun Heming (male), the total second prize went to Zhu Tiexi (male), the total third prize went to Tai Zhixing (male), first place in the first stage went to Sun Heming (male), first place in the second stage went to Xia Fuqi (male), first place in the third stage went to Fan Cunru (male), first place in the fourth stage went to Zhang Fugen (male), first place in the fifth stage went to Li Kunquan (male), first place in the sixth stage went to Zhong Zhixing (male), first place in the seventh stage went to Zhou Qingliu (male), first place in the eighth stage went to Zhu Zhiyi (female), first place in the ninth stage went to Ni Yuji (male), first place in the tenth stage went to Zhu Tiexian (male), first place in the eleventh stage went to Zhou Chenluan (male), and first place in the twelfth stage went to Fan Cunjian (female). The judges signed and announced the results. Awards were then given.

Award Ceremony and Entertainment: The awards were presented by Mrs. Li. Every participating child received a prize. On the same day, the Ministry of Interior presented a large silver shield. After the awards, the People's Opera Troupe performed Beijing opera to add to the entertainment.

Baoshan County Plans to Dredge the Meipu River 127

The Meipu River in Meipu Township, Baoshan First District, has been severely silted up due to years of neglect.桂屢中, the township head, recognizing that transportation is quite inconvenient, submitted a request to the First District Office in mid-June to forward it to the Baoshan County Government for dredging to facilitate transportation. The County Government then instructed Sun, the former district chief of the First District, to work with Huang, the former director of the Construction Bureau, to make an overall estimate. However, District Chief Sun and Director Huang left their positions one after another, and the project was not realized. Now, District Chief Wang of the First District, together with Qian, Director of the Construction Bureau, have carefully planned and estimated that it will cost over 12,000 silver dollars. However, the district only has over 9,000 yuan of water conservancy funds, which is insufficient. Township Head Gui has been negotiating with farmers along the river to borrow the shortfall, and it is said that an agreement has been reached. Construction is expected to begin soon.

This Year's Wheat Production in the City is Relatively High 128

Survey by the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs

The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs previously formulated survey forms on the production status of large and small wheat, instructing each district committee in the city to diligently complete and report them. The statistics have now been compiled. The total production volume for the entire city this year is estimated to be over 350,000 dan. The varieties in each district are broadly divided into two types: awned and awnless, with red and white skin colors and good powder quality. However, the average yield is higher than in other regions. The reason for this is attributed to the suitability of the soil and climate, as well as the proximity to the city, which allows for a more adequate application of fertilizer. Therefore, the average yield per mu is over three shi for the highest and at least one and a half shi for the lowest.

Mishaps on the Upper Yangtze River Shipping Routes 130

The Xiushan Steamer Sinks: The water level in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, especially in central Hunan, is the shallowest. Above Chenglingji, it is only six to seven feet deep. The Jardine Matheson Company's Hunan liners have changed to using shallow-draft vessels like the Xiushan. Last week, the Xiushan set off from Hankou carrying cargo and passengers. When it reached Chenglingji, the ship ran aground. The shipowner issued a distress signal. The Hankou branch of Jardine Matheson immediately dispatched a tug to rescue it. However, the water level receded daily, and the Xiushan, due to carrying a lot of cargo, ran aground very deeply. The riverbed is full of reefs. Multiple small vessels tried to tow it for days without success. Yesterday, news reached Shanghai that the bottom of the Xiushan had been breached, and river water was entering the hold. The ship was sinking. The passengers on board have already been transferred to small boats to Changsha. It is not yet known if there were any injuries. However, only a small portion of the cargo has been unloaded, and the rest has sunk with the ship, resulting in a huge loss. The Xiushan is one of the four new shallow-draft vessels of Jardine Matheson's Upper Yangtze fleet. The ship's hull is very good and can carry over 180 tons of cargo.

The Jintang Steamer Escapes Danger: The company's Chongqing shallow-draft vessel, the Jintang, replaced the 1,000-ton Wantong to sail to Yichang and Chongqing, carrying a large amount of cotton yarn and piece goods. When the ship reached Shishou, it encountered bandit boats. To avoid the bandits' guns and artillery, the shipowner deliberately ran aground on the Shishou River, making it impossible to sail. Fearing that the bandits would board the ship to rob and kidnap the crew and passengers, the shipowner, to protect the lives of everyone on board and avoid being kidnapped, ordered the sailors to throw 130 pieces of cotton yarn and some piece goods, worth over 60,000 yuan, into the Yangtze River to reduce the weight. After the goods were discarded, the Jintang was able to move. The bandits were about to board the ship on small boats to rob when a warship arrived, saving the Jintang from danger. It was heard yesterday that the ship has been towed out and is heading to Chongqing, but the loss of goods is estimated to be about 70,000 yuan.

The Xinyunnan Steamer is Robbed: Yesterday, a British ship arrived in Shanghai from Yichang. The crew members told reporters that the Xinyunnan, which was transporting special tax goods, was robbed by bandits at Tiaoguan. The ship also ran aground to avoid the bandits' gunfire. There were over a hundred bandits who boarded the ship and looted not only the cargo but even the ship's accessories, such as anchors and chains, leaving nothing behind. The twelve soldiers escorting the ship and the crew members were all kidnapped by the bandits and are still missing. The rivers in Sichuan are full of bandits, making it extremely difficult to navigate.

New Shipping Routes Opened in Eastern Zhejiang 131

Chinese businessmen Bao Dating and others raised 500,000 yuan to establish Kaili Company to open new shipping routes from Shanghai to Xiangshan, passing through Ninghai, Huanglong, Sizhou, Shengshan, Jushan, Daishan, and Shenjiamen Gaoting. They have purchased a Japanese ship, rebuilt it into a passenger ship, and named it Kaiyuan. It is expected to start operating within three weeks. For now, there will be only one class of cabins. The fare from Shanghai to Huanglong, Sizhou, and Shengshan is 3 yuan per person. The fare to Jushan and Daishan is 2 yuan, and the remaining stops are 1.5 yuan. The freight rate for cargo and water is 5 to 8 yuan per ton. During the incense season, it will also travel to Shantuan. In the future, another ship will be added as the business develops.

The Gonghe Steamer's Comprador Drives Workers Ashore 133

The Shanghai Bureau of Social Affairs Cables the Hankou Bureau of Social Affairs for Mediation

The Jardine Matheson Company's Gonghe steamer, which operates on the Yangtze River, has replaced its comprador. At that time, Director Pan of the Shanghai Bureau of Social Affairs sent staff member Wang Bin to mediate. He warned Shen not to dismiss the workers without cause and publicly instructed all the workers to remain on the ship and continue working as usual, pending a resolution of the matter. However, the next day (the 5th) in the evening, as the ship was about to set sail for Hankou, Comprador Shen suddenly ordered a certain Gu to gather over a hundred armed thugs and tightly guard the Zhuang Yuanda Shuntai pier, as if facing a major enemy. The Fastest Steamer on the Huangpu River 134

Shanghai's Third and Fourth Ferry Boats

Speed of 12 Nautical Miles Per Hour

Since the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities took over the Pukou Ferry (i.e., from the Bund on Nanjing Road to Donggou), it has been determined to make improvements and to facilitate transportation without the goal of profit. Last year, the newly built Ferry Boats No. 1 and 2 were put into service, with beautiful, comfortable, and sturdy equipment. Their high speed made travel very convenient for passengers. Recently, Ferry Boats No. 3 and 4 were added to expand the routes and operate to Gaoqiao. They were built by the He Xing Factory and have now been completed. The supervisors and technicians from the Bureau of Public Utilities conducted trial runs in the Tangwan area, and the highest speed reached 12 nautical miles per hour. The fastest ships on the Huangpu River in the past were those of the Da Lai Company and the Dredging Bureau, but none could reach 12 nautical miles per hour. The municipal ferries are the first to set this record. These ferries usually only need 10 nautical miles per hour, but in the lower reaches of the Huangpu River, when the wind and waves are high, they can operate at full power without being affected and without any delays. It is said that the Bureau has scheduled an official trial run on December 15th and has invited representatives from relevant organizations to visit the ship.

The Songhu Railway Branch Station is Scheduled to Relocate to the East End of Baoshan Road 135

Track Change on the Night of the 12th

Traffic Stopped for Six Hours

The Songhu Railway crosses Zhabei Baoshan Road with a gate. Since the introduction of steam trains this year, there are more than 70 round trips per day. The gate is frequently opened and closed, which not only obstructs traffic but also affects municipal development. The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities and the Bureau of Public Works, in view of this, suggested relocating the Songhu branch station to the east end of Baoshan Road. The proposal was submitted by the Municipal Government to the Ministry of Railways for instructions. It is learned that the railway authorities have received the Ministry of Railways' approval for the relocation and have scheduled the track change and laying work to begin from 12 midnight on the 12th to 6 a.m. on the 13th of this month. During this six-hour period, vehicles traveling to and from the Baoshan Road gate must stop. The Bureau of Public Utilities has sent a letter to the Public Security Bureau to inform the relevant district police stations to pay attention.

Resolution of the Japanese Crew Beating Vendor Case 137

Japanese Ships of Nisshin Company frequently assault passengers. Last time, a servant in the Xiangyang Maru beat a passenger from Anqing to Wuhu to death because he didn’t have a ticket. The Wuhu Local Court already sentenced the assailant to six months imprisonment. The Comprador of the Xiangyang Maru already spent over 2,000 yuan to try to settle with the family, but a settlement has not been reached and compensations have not been paid. Before that case could be settled, another incident happened: the chef of the Dali Maru assaulted a vendor. The ship already arrived in Shanghai yesterday. It is claimed that a vendor, Chen Wenfa, boarded the ship in Datong and went into the kitchen to warm himself by the fire. Chef Yu Azhang and others saw him and drove him away. But because he didn’t leave, Yu and others beat and hung him for a whole night. The vendor suffered grave injuries. When the ship arrived in Wuhu, the passengers, unhappy, turned Yu Azhang and two other suspects over to the Public Security Bureau to be sent to the court. The court immediately decided that the injured would be treated in the hospital and the head of the kitchen, Fan, would be responsible for the four yuan medical fee per day until the vendor was discharged from the hospital. The three suspects would be imprisoned in the courthouse and released when the vendor’s injuries were healed. The Ship’s Management will take responsibility for all costs. The ship left as scheduled this morning.

The Municipal Bureau of Public Works Pays Attention to Factory Housing Equipment 138

The Municipal Bureau of Public Works, in view of the fact that there are many ordinary houses in the city that have been converted into temporary factories, and that public safety equipment is often lacking, making them unable to withstand unexpected dangers, invited representatives from the Public Security Bureau and the Bureau of Social Affairs to a meeting on the 18th of last month to discuss the matter. It was decided at the meeting to send personnel to conduct investigations and stipulate three rectification measures: (1) All rear doors must be kept open at all times during working hours and must not be locked. Factories without rear doors must add them within a time limit. (2) The factory staircases must be sturdy, and each house must have at least two staircases. If several houses are connected to form a single factory, the number of staircases should be increased according to the situation. If it is necessary to add fire escapes due to the large number of people, they should be ordered to be added. (3) If it is possible to install fire hydrants, they should be ordered to install them. Otherwise, they should be ordered to equip a certain number of fire buckets. It is said that these measures are only temporary solutions. Currently, personnel are being sent to start inspections in the jurisdiction of the four districts of Zhabei, while other thorough rectification measures are being drafted. Once they are finalized, the city's factories will be divided into areas for sequential investigation. The factories that have already been inspected are as follows: Changji Oil Cake Factory in Panjiawan, Xiangfeng Flower Shop on Guangfu Road, Changxing Dali Military Uniform Factory on Baoshan Road, Dahua Military Uniform Factory on Zhongxing Road, Dachang Military Uniform Factory on Xinmin Road, Huafeng Military Uniform Factory on Jinling Road, Rongchangxiang Military Uniform Factory in Wanan Lane, Baotong Road, and Fuchang Military Uniform Factory in Sanyang Lane, Sanyang Road.

It is also heard that he has been hired by the Daxin Silk and Satin Store as the chief of the store's Art New Design Department.

Lawsuit Involving Residents and Landlord in Jiyi Lane 146

The Point of Contention

Is the Validity of the Lease

The Judge Adjourns for Pronouncement of Judgement

Hoping That Both Parties Reconcile

During the summer, Ye Shantao, the owner of the Yizun Company, instructed its manager, the British firm Tonghe Yanghang, to notify the residents of Jiyi Lane on Shanxi Road to move out in order to rebuild. The residents formed an association to negotiate with the owner regarding rent increases and lease extensions. However, the owner later regretted the agreement and sold the property to the Hexing Company for 1.1 million yuan, causing the tenants to receive repeated eviction notices from both the old and new landlords, treating the lease as waste paper. The residents, numbering seventeen households, jointly hired lawyer Chen Tingrui to file a lawsuit with the Special District Court, requesting a judgment to confirm that the lease agreement with Yizun Company and Ye Shantao was valid and binding on Hexing Company. Yizun also hired lawyer Lu Zhongliang, who, in addition to denying the establishment of the lease agreement, filed a counterclaim to recover over 8,000 taels of rent owed by the tenants. Hexing Company also hired lawyers Cai and Li to file a counterclaim against the tenants, demanding they move out. Judge Xu Wenrong held a hearing. As reported previously, testimony was heard yesterday morning. Xinmin Hotel, a tenant, stated that the lease contract was prepared by Tonghe Yanghang and distributed to each tenant with the door number and name filled in. The tenants signed and stamped the contracts. Tonghe never came to pick up the contracts from Xinmin. Inside Jiyi Lane, according to the agreed-upon rent increase level, houses inside the lane were to have a 30% increase. The defendant initially wanted to increase the rent for Xinmin by 50%, similar to the increase for houses facing the street. After several discussions, the defendant insisted on a 35% increase, so Xinmin did not immediately stamp the contract. This does not mean that they disagreed with all the terms. Lu Shaotang was then questioned about the negotiation process with the landlord. Lu stated that he was sent by the tenant association as a representative to assist the landlord to negotiate. He went to Tonghe Yanghang to seek the owner's opinion. According to them, the owner insisted that street-facing houses be increased by 50% and houses inside the lane by 30%. If a house collapsed within five years, the owner would not be responsible. Furthermore, the tenants were not allowed to sublet during these five years. If all tenants agreed, the demolition would be delayed for five years. Some three or four tenants did not fully agree with the terms, but Tonghe insisted that all tenants agree, or they would not sign the lease. Because of the disagreement among the tenants, he resigned from mediation, and Zhang Xingzhai continued to negotiate with the landlord, he said. The owner of Mohuaxuan, a tenant, stated that the rent collector, Mr. Ying, instructed them to ask Lu to negotiate with the landlord because Ying said Lu was closest to Ye Shantao. Lu's resignation was due to Tonghe's statement to the tenant association on September 19th, announcing the cancellation of the agreed-upon lease. Because they felt that they could not face the tenants if they suddenly canceled the agreement, he resigned. Zhang Xingzhai then described his negotiation with the landlord after Lu's resignation. The tenants saw the landlord's letter canceling the previous agreement, in which he did not agree to extend the lease for five years. They then reduced the request to one year, during which time there would be no demolition or rent increase. Unexpectedly, two collapses occurred in houses inside the lane, and the landlord was even more unwilling to delay the demolition even for a moment. Several tenants who heard Zhang mention the collapse of the houses immediately clarified that what collapsed was a shed built by the tenants themselves, and only one rubber sheet was damaged, not the main beams or rafters. The arguments then began. Lawyer Chen Tingrui, representing the plaintiff, spoke for the longest time, stating that the first defendant, Yizun Company's, counterclaim for rent arrears was unreasonable. The plaintiffs were not refusing to pay rent and were willing to pay according to the new rent increase. The money was stored in the bank because they did not come to collect it. Therefore, their counterclaim should not stand. The second defendant, Hexing Company's, counterclaim for eviction should be a preliminary hearing. Moreover, the purpose of their counterclaim was different from the main suit, so there was no need to argue it. The reasons for the plaintiff's request for confirmation of the lease agreement and the binding of the second defendant to the contract were sufficient. The contract had been established, and some tenants had already paid rent at the new rate, so it had already taken effect. Tonghe's letter on September 19th also acknowledged the existence of this contract and requested its cancellation. The ink was not yet dry, and the words were still in the air, so how could they go back on their word? The reasons for their request for cancellation were not related to the plaintiff. Although it seemed reasonable to say that they could overturn the contract because they had not signed it, a review of the nature of the contract showed that there was no room for cancellation. Since the contract was prepared by Tonghe, it was no different from Tonghe making an offer to the tenants. According to the law, if the offeree did not express refusal of the offer, the offeror should be bound by the offer. In this case, the plaintiffs had not only not refused but had also obeyed the order to stamp the contract, so the defendant could not be exempt. Therefore, he specifically requested that the court confirm the validity of the lease and order the second defendant to be bound by it, he said. Lawyer representing Yizun replied that the disputed contract had not been signed by the defendant and was still in the hands of the plaintiff, so it had not been established and could be revoked. As for the offer, the plaintiff had offered the defendant a five-year no-rent-increase and five-year no-demolition, while Tonghe had proposed no subletting. The tenants had different opinions on this, which was tantamount to expressing refusal, and the defendant could also cancel the previous agreement. Furthermore, two collapses had occurred, indicating that the house was old. In short, since the plaintiff could not produce a contract signed by both parties, he should request the dismissal of his claim. The defendant's counterclaim for rent arrears. The deposit slips presented by the plaintiffs in this hearing were incomplete, and some had no name or the amount was insufficient to cover the arrears. It was clear that the plaintiffs wanted to use the lawsuit to delay the payment of rent. If they secretly moved away after owing so much, the defendant would suffer greatly. He requested an immediate judgment and a declaration of provisional execution, he said. Lawyer for Hexing Company argued that Hexing's counterclaim was related to the main suit. The plaintiff's argument regarding the level of jurisdiction was wrong and should be rejected. Hexing was being considerate of those who had to move and was extending the deadline by one month to the end of February next year. Xu, the judge, adjourned the debate, scheduled the pronouncement of judgment for the 16th, and advised both parties to reconcile outside of court during this period.

Death From Smoking 157

Jiang Yang's Misfortune Comes from Matches

The skin and flesh were even stuck to the undershirt, and her body was covered in blood. Although the doctor treated her, the injuries were too severe, and she died the night before last. The funeral was held yesterday, and the relatives were deeply saddened.

Today, Xiuzhai ordered me and his younger brother to take the two children by boat from the Xinguang Wharf to Pudong, then take rickshaws back to the old Baidu and hand them over to Lin for export to Fujian to avoid the eyes and ears of others. Unexpectedly, the case was suddenly solved, etc. According to Zhao Gengsheng, he was eleven years old, from Taizhou, and lived at No. 111, Xiaocaitang, Sanjiaojie, Nanshi. They were playing at the entrance last Saturday, and he (referring to Zhao Gengsheng) suddenly came up to us and said that there was a living monkey performance nearby and told us to go and watch it quickly, etc. We believed it to be true and followed him. After turning several corners, an adult came and then met another adult (referring to Liu Maolang), who forcibly pulled us into a rickshaw and took us to a hotel to live in. We had no relatives and cried loudly. Today, these people brought us here again, and we don't know why, etc. After obtaining the confession, the district chief sent detective Zhang Yong to arrest Zhao Xiuzhai and Lin Zhongyu, who planned to sell the two children, both had fled. He also went to the homes of the two children to inquire.
